# Project Overview

- Project: `futures_intraday_model`.
- Purpose: intraday futures research pipeline using Databento continuous-contract 1-minute OHLCV data.
- Status framing: research and walk-forward validation only; this is not live-trading or production readiness.
- Project outline authority: use `PROJECT_OUTLINE.md` for objective, layout, phase order, runnable phase commands, acceptance checks, and stop conditions.
- Repo guidance authority: use `AGENTS.md` for agent workflow, safety rules, and final-response format.
- Handoff role: this file is mutable cross-run state. Reconcile all material claims against current repo files, reports, command output, and `git status` before acting.
- Solo Codex files: keep `AGENTS.md`, `PROJECT_OUTLINE.md`, and `CODEX_HANDOFF.md` only; do not create `PROJECT_STATE.md`, `research/JOURNAL.md`, or parallel handoff/state files unless explicitly requested.
- History note: this file was compacted on 2026-06-30 from the prior chronological handoff log into a standing-state handoff. Use git history only if exact older run text is needed.

# Superseded Context

- Any older handoff bullet or fresh-thread prompt that says the selected next thesis is `tier1_core_directional_baseline_v1` is historical only. Current repo evidence has that hypothesis `REJECTED` with no next allowed actions; it must not drive current work.

Source/docs/tests-only changes: updated `scripts/validation/run_alpha_discovery.py`, `tests/validation/test_run_alpha_discovery.py`, `PROJECT_OUTLINE.md`, and this handoff; `RUN_ALPHA_DISCOVERY.bat` behavior remains a thin launcher. The runner now reads generated discovery JSON when present and exposes `candidate_decision`, `candidate_passed`, `candidate_stopped`, `command_succeeded`, and `target_smoke_is_tradability_proof=false`. `DISCOVERY_PASS` is classified as candidate pass; any `STOP_*` JSON decision is classified as candidate stop even if the Phase 9 subprocess exits `0`; missing JSON/MD outputs remain `DISCOVERY_RUN_REVIEW_REQUIRED`; top-level successful wrapper output now uses `status=RUNNER_COMPLETED` and `runner_completed=true` so a wrapper completion cannot be mistaken for candidate success. - 2026-07-04 implemented the source/tests-only gated batch runner for alpha discovery. Added `run_alpha_discovery.bat`, `scripts/validation/run_alpha_discovery.py`, `configs/alpha_discovery_runner.example.json`, and focused tests in `tests/validation/test_run_alpha_discovery.py`. The `.bat` only sets the repo root, checks Python, and launches the Python orchestrator with ignored logs under `logs/alpha_discovery/`. The orchestrator supports `preflight`, `source-tests`, `discovery-packet`, `discovery-run`, and `review` modes; it fail-closes on template configs, missing registry/status files, non-`CANDIDATE` discovery-start status, `wfa_allowed=true`, prior discovery trial-status evidence, stale expected outputs, expected outputs that are not git-ignored, missing target-policy contract fields, path-favorable targets claiming `fixed_horizon_exit` compatibility, non-pytest source-test commands, or discovery commands outside `scripts.phase9_research.*`. `discovery-run` requires both `--approve-discovery-run` and the exact configured approval token, then runs one bounded discovery command and reviews expected JSON/MD if written; it does not advance to confirmation, locked smoke, WFA/modeling, Phase 8, tuning, promotion, registry/status mutation, staging, commit, push, paper, or live action. The config template is intentionally marked `template=true` so it cannot operate until copied and filled for a real registered candidate. Validation run so far: `python -m pytest -q -p no:cacheprovider tests/validation/test_run_alpha_discovery.py` (`8 passed`), `python -m pytest -q -p no:cacheprovider tests/validation/test_run_alpha_discovery.py tests/validation/test_target_policy_contract.py` (`14 passed`), and `run_alpha_discovery.bat --config configs\alpha_discovery_runner.example.json --mode preflight` failed closed as expected with `config is marked template=true`; the generated log under `logs/alpha_discovery/` is ignored and `git status --short -- data reports logs` is clean. Added `scripts/validation/target_policy_contract.py` with explicit contract metadata for this target: payoff basis `path_favorable_excursion`, entry rule `next_bar_open`, horizon `30` bars, label threshold `future favorable path excursion > round_turn_cost_ticks + min_profit_ticks`, and required compatible policy basis `first_touch_path_capture`; the gate marks `fixed_horizon_exit` as incompatible and non-decisive for economic approval/rejection. Added first-touch simulation helpers covering TP-only, SL-only, horizon-exit, same-bar ambiguous, and stop-first conservative handling. Updated `scripts/validation/run_opening_range_acceptance_wfa_materialization.py` so future materialization reports carry the target-policy contract metadata. - 2026-07-04 created `docs/opening_range_acceptance_continuation_30m_v1_low_tick_rule_attribution.md` plus `scripts/phase8_model_selection/analyze_low_tick_rule_attribution.py` and focused tests in `tests/phase8_model_selection/test_low_tick_rule_attribution.py` to explain which rules caused low fixed-exit realized ticks for `opening_range_acceptance_continuation_30m_v1`. This was analysis-only using existing WFA predictions, the executed-trades CSV, ES 2024 materialized bars, `configs/costs.yaml`, and existing target/policy rules; no WFA/modeling rerun, diagnostics rerun, tuning, stop/target backtest, cost-model change, registry/status mutation, promotion, generated-artifact cleanup, staging, commit, push, paper, or live execution was performed. Key attribution facts: prediction rows `72539`; candidate trades before non-overlap `66473` (`91.6%` of prediction rows); executed trades `2668`; overlap-blocked candidates `63805`; candidate fixed-exit median `0.00` ticks and mean `-0.26`; executed fixed-exit median `0.00` ticks and mean `-0.05`; blocked fixed-exit median `0.00` ticks and mean `-0.26`, so non-overlap did not create the low-tick problem. Path-label target-direction matches were materially better than mismatches (`+4.53` mean fixed-exit ticks vs `-11.86`), but the target labels path opportunity while the evaluated policy exits at the fixed 30-minute open. Executed path MFE median was `9.00` ticks, median giveback to fixed exit was `9.00` ticks, `831/2668` trades (`31.1%`) had MFE `>=5` ticks but fixed-exit realized ticks `<=2`, and `532/2668` (`19.9%`) had MFE `>=8` ticks but fixed-exit realized ticks `<=2`. Model confidence deciles did not produce a monotonic fixed-exit edge, and acceptance-distance buckets did not rescue the fixed-exit result. Report conclusion: the strategy's low realized ticks are mainly explained by a target/policy mismatch: the target rewarded favorable path excursion after opening-range acceptance, while the tested policy had no take-profit/stop or first-touch execution rule and simply exited at the 30-minute open; no probability, margin, or expected-tick threshold filtered weak signals. Validation passed: `python -m pytest -q -p no:cacheprovider tests/phase8_model_selection/test_low_tick_rule_attribution.py` (`5 passed`). Exact next recommended step: review `docs/opening_range_acceptance_continuation_30m_v1_low_tick_rule_attribution.md` before any separate stop/target first-touch feasibility packet, cost-model sensitivity change, `RETIRED` registry/status disposition, tuning, WFA/modeling, promotion, staging, commit, push, paper, or live decision.
- 2026-07-04 created `docs/opening_range_acceptance_continuation_30m_v1_trade_tick_excursion_analysis.md` plus `scripts/phase8_model_selection/analyze_trade_tick_excursions.py` and focused tests in `tests/phase8_model_selection/test_trade_tick_excursion_analysis.py` to analyze the 2,668 executed single-target policy trades using only the existing trades CSV, ES 2024 materialized WFA bars, and `configs/costs.yaml`. No WFA/modeling rerun, diagnostics rerun, tuning, promotion, registry/status mutation, generated-artifact cleanup, staging, commit, push, paper, or live execution was performed. The analysis validates exact joins for all 2,668 signal, entry, and exit bars; uses ES tick size `0.25`, tick value `$12.50`, and current round-turn cost `$29.50` / `2.36` ticks; computes realized gross ticks, current-cost net ticks, position-adjusted 30m max favorable/adverse excursion, TP/SL reach rates, same-size TP/SL outcomes, and a full TP/SL grid with both-touched rows marked ambiguous because OHLC bars cannot prove first-touch order. Key report facts: total realized gross `-141.00` ticks / `$-1762.50`; total current-cost net `-6437.48` ticks / `$-80468.50`; max favorable excursion `<=2` ticks for `447/2668` trades (`16.8%`); realized gross `<=2` ticks for `1568/2668` trades (`58.8%`); adverse excursion `>=3` ticks for `2269/2668` trades (`85.0%`); same-size 2-tick TP/SL had `247` TP-only, `259` SL-only, `2162` both-touched ambiguous, and `0` neither. Interpretation recorded in the report: the policy did not fail only because costs were high; realized gross edge was near flat/slightly negative, many trades realized too little, and adverse excursion was common enough that any stop/target rescue needs first-touch validation rather than OHLC-only assumptions. Validation passed: `python -m pytest -q -p no:cacheprovider tests/phase8_model_selection/test_trade_tick_excursion_analysis.py` (`4 passed`). Exact next recommended step: review `docs/opening_range_acceptance_continuation_30m_v1_trade_tick_excursion_analysis.md` before any separate `RETIRED` registry/status disposition, cost-model sensitivity change, stop/target policy test, tuning, WFA/modeling, promotion, staging, commit, push, paper, or live decision.
